  37. A while ago I posted the below negative review out of sheer disappointment and quite honestly, panic, due to the stains I acquired along my lash line....however....I feel the need to take a moment to re-review as I eventually figured out a key component. If you choose to give this product a shot you MUST make sure the petroleum-based product you coat the skin around your eye with before starting the tinting process is heavy on the petroleum side. Yes...there are varying petroleum intensities and THAT is where I went horribly wrong. You'll need either straight-up vaseline or a thick balm (non-minty of course). Co. Bigelow (at Bath & Body Works) produces a lovely rose fragranced balm which I've discovered works splendidly. To apply the balm I use an actual small angled paint brush (generally available at any craft store). This is a tremendous help in applying the petroleum with true accuracy so as to avoid getting it on your lashes. Allow yourself enough time to move slowly. And ideally, especially if it's your first attempt at it, don't plan on going anywhere afterward. It's just safer and takes some of the pressure off because it IS a little awkward - expect a bit of a learning curve. AnyWHO...good luck and remember, take your time. ;-)<br /><br />Let me first start by saying that I have never before taken the time to post an unfavorable review. But for this, I simply had to. I absolutely do not recommend this product. In the past I have always just bit the bullet and gone into a spa to have my lashes done professionally. But after reading several of the reviews posted for this product, I thought, 'Hey! This may be a great solution, not to mention quite a savings!' Boy was I wrong. I followed what was recommended on the box, as well as followed tips posted by others, but was very disappointed to find that not only did my lashes take on the color only minimally, but I was left with awful stains lining both my upper and lower lash lines...not in a nice \\"semi-eyeliner\\" kind of way, but in an \\"I've been crying for the last hour\\" kind of way. I sit here typing this review feeling like the RCA dog with a lovely ring around my left eye. I'm not even going to attempt to do my right....forget it!   66. EDIT 8/5/2011: Yes, this is a true \\"dye\\", and is permanent in that it does darken the lashes significantly and slowly wears off over four to six weeks. It will withstand soap, lotion, ointments, mascara, etc., so it is definitely worth doing if you have eyelashes that are not very dark. Read my original post below for must do's and don'ts. The reason I am editing my review is that I have stumbled across an easy way to quickly remove all dye stains from your hands, which are almost inevitable as no one can really work with those silly hair dye gloves on. I dyed my lashes today, and made a much greater mess of my hands than usual. Really dark stains on almost every finger, including the nails. I thought that I would soak my hands, and the try to file off the top layers of my skin with a nail file (does work, but not sufficiently to rob a bank!). Then, I had to mix up some hair bleach for my daughter, who hates her dark arm hair. I had some of the bleach (Sally Hansen creme bleach for the body) left over and thought, why not see if that takes the dye stains out? AND IT DID - COMPLETELY!! I left the creme on them for about 5 minutes, and it had taken most of the stains off and reduced the really dark ones until they were faint. So I reapplied the bleach on those areas again for a few more minutes and all the stains were totally gone, even around and underneath my fingernails. It didn't leave the skin dry or noticeably lightened where the bleach was applied, although it might if you left it on too long or have dark skin - just be careful to apply precisely to the stain in that case. You'd have to do one hand at a time, but the bleach stays good for quite a long time after you mix it up, and you can reuse the same bleach on the other hand. As most of the body hair bleach brands use the same materials, I'm sure that Jolene or any other similar hair bleach system (using a dry powder bleach you mix with a creme activator) will work. ORIGINAL REVIEW:I have had my lashes tinted at the salon over many years. I was blessed with thick, long, naturally curly lashes, of a medium brown color (I'm a redhead). So much so that I could not wear any mascara that added length or thickened, as it made it look like I had a bad set of false eyelashes. So, I tinted. Now, at 50, my lashes are still long, but not nearly as thick, and have faded to a lighter brown, with the tips almost invisible. I can wear mascara, but still feel that it looks like false eyelashes - I just want to see what I have naturally, so tinting is still my preference. It is hard to find salons that still offer lash tinting, and the price is prohibitive ($40, and a tip is expected). So, I tried the do-it-at-home kits, starting with Roux, the old standby, purchased at a local beauty supply store for about $32. Roux's kit is hard to use, as both the developer (1st solution applied) and the color (applied on top of developer) are thin liquids. However, on the plus side, Roux includes a stain remover vial as well, which works fairly well (but never gets the dye off completely in all areas). Recently, I accidentally spilled the color vial in my Roux kit, and would have had to purchase a whole new kit to replace it. Rather than just re-order Roux, I perused other possibilities online and found this product on Amazon, 28 Day Mascara. Reading the reviews, I saw that there was a large disagreement between reviewers, with some stating that there was no color added to their lashes at all. I decided to go for it anyway, and am glad I did. Yes, this product DOES WORK!! I am sitting here looking at very black, completely colored lashes, top and bottom. The thicker, gel consistency of the colorant made it easier to apply than the Roux solution, so less staining. However, there was still that eye-burning sensation when I got too close to the root on the upper lids. I want my lashes died from root to tip, so that is something I just have to put up with. The reason I give it 4 stars instead of 5 is that this kit is still not perfect, there will be stains and stinging no matter how careful you are, and the process can still be improved. I don't know why other reviewers found this kit didn't work for them, excluding those who thought tinting meant a mascara-like thickening and lengthening miracle. I can only conclude that they did something to prevent the product from performing as it did for me. Here are some of the possible mistakes to avoid: 1. Did not properly clean their lashes prior to tinting. You cannot have ANYTHING on your lashes - no remover, no moisturizer, no soap residue, nada! If you take off your mascara with a remover, and then expect to tint your eyelashes, it will not adhere as there is a physical barrier on your lashes. I took off my mascara, then washed my face, paying particular attention to my lashes, using actual soap. Not a facial cream, not a makeup remover, not even a moisturizing soap, just plain soap. Yes it dried out my skin, but as soon as I was done with the tinting, I moisturized the heck out of my face. 2. Used too much Vaseline, or got Vaseline on their lashes. This would explain the reviewers complaining about how the tint didn't take to their lower lashes. Vaseline is insidious. It gets on everything it touches. I knew that I could not use Vaseline under my lower lashes without getting some on the lashes, thus defeating the whole intent of coloring them. My lower lashes touch the skin below the eyelid, and any Vaseline would travel up higher as I tried to tint them. Then the Vaseline would contaminate the swab, keeping the developer from properly coating the lower lashes. Just skip the Vaseline/paper cover step entirely, go slowly and carefully, and accept that you will have some minor staining for a day or so. Have a clean, dry swab at the ready to quickly remove any staining blobs as they occur - the faster you clean it off the less it will stain. 3. Did not use proper lighting or magnification. If you are in a brightly lit room (good bathroom light), and use a makeup mirror that magnifies, you will see that your lashes are actually longer than you think. It is hard to see them just looking in a mirror - you need the good light (you're tinting your lashes because they are pale, so without good light you won't see them). You cannot tint them and then expect to suddenly see them clearly without good light and magnification. You may have tinted your lower lashes successfully, but not appreciate that fact as you are not using a sufficient light or magnification to see them. The angle at which your lower lashes curl makes them hard to see regardless of their color, so I suspect that some reviewers reported less than expected results merely because they were not looking at their newly tinted lashes properly. Doing the lower lashes on one eye first, you can then compare them to the other eye's lower lashes, and you will see that, if you did it correctly, the tinted lashes are much darker than the untinted ones. 4. Did not use glasses if they need them. I wear reading glasses, and I was able to wear them WHILE I tinted my lashes, and also used a magnifying makeup mirror (one with a stand). Sliding the glasses down a little on my nose, and angling the mirror so that I was looking down into it when I tilted my head, I had room to maneuver the swab soaked with the developer underneath my glasses, so between them and my eye. Using the mirror as well gave me a complete, clear view of each lash on my lower lid. I was able to reach the upper lashes from above my glasses. Every now and then, I bumped my glasses with the swab, but they're made of glass, so I knew nothing in the kit could damage the lenses. I just ignored the small amount of liquid on my glasses until I was done with my lashes, and then wiped it off. 5. Did not go slowly enough or carefully enough. You need to devote sufficient timeto the whole tinting process, and to do only one set of lashes (upper right, lower right, upper left, lower left), at a time. Count on at least 30 to 45 minutes, and do one of the four sets of eyelashes at a time from start to finish. The instructions state you should apply the first solution 2 to 3 times over each lash. Then you need to wait one minute (or a little longer is OK), for the developer to dry. It has to dry! And it has to saturate each lash completely, hence the reapplications before moving on to the coloring step. Don't be stingy - make sure that the swab is really wet and re-wet it for each of the 3 applications you will do prior to using the colorant gel. 6. Did not use a small enough, or well enough designed applicator for the colorant gel. The swabs included in the kit are fine for applying the developer solution, the first step. But they are not so good for applying the second step, the colorant gel, because this solution is the one that stings, and the one that stains. I had intended to use an old mascara wand, but realized that this wouldn't work with my method (the under-the-glasses application) as it was just too big and thick. So I used one of my son's braces brushes - a disposable mini brush (half an inch, if that) on a two inch handle (just happened to see one in the bathroom drawer and had a Light Bulb Moment). This brush is made of wire and short bristles, and you can bend the wire as well, to create an angle you wouldn't get from a mascara wand. Yes, that brush is now kept in the kit's box, so he doesn't use it by mistake, but the tinting solution cleaned off completely. These tiny brushes are available in the toothpaste/floss section of any drug store in packs of multiples - much cheaper than the mascara wands, and much easier to use for the lower lashes than anything else. They work great on the upper lashes too, but those are the easier lashes to tint anyway. My lashes are extremely black now, and I have washed them a couple of times and have applied moisturizers several times. I used the left over Roux stain remover, and it worked fairly well for the stains I ended up with from the 28 Day Mascara tinting. There is, however, a vague, bluish grey color under my lower lashes, which I know will fade away completely over the next day or two. Until then, that's why I have concealer. You can purchase tint remover for your skin at any beauty supply store, for when you use hair dye, and it's not very expensive. If you use a swab and are careful, these will work to remove or at least reduce the tinting stains. However, if you clean the stains off immediately with a clean, dry swab (no stain remover until you are done tinting) as they occur, there will be less staining to deal with at the end. I don't know how long this 28 Day Mascara tint job will last, and will update this review if I think the product didn't hold up as long as the Roux. Usually after the third week I think about re-tinting, so I'll see if 28 Day Mascara lasts that long.

  194. I am amazed by how well this product works! I have never written a review before, but I am so pleased with this product that I have to share it. I just used it a few hours ago. I have pale, light brown/blonde lashes and this is the first time that I have used any product like this. I was doubtful that it would work, but this product does exactly what it claims: it tints lashes black. It will not make you look as if you are wearing mascara, which thickens and adds length to lashes, but the tint will make your lashes a dark, rich black color. If you have dark black lashes already then this product will probably not do very much for you, but it is great for lighter lashes. I was also very pleased to find out that this product is made in Sweden, which lessened my fear that it would damage or hurt my eyes. This is a great, highly effective product, and if you use it correctly it will absolutely work. I think that any negative reviews are due to people expecting a mascara-like product or those who do not use it correctly. I am so happy with the results, here are a few tips that I think will help you achieve great results too: 1) First I thoroughly cleaned and dried my lashes, using a mild cleanser (there cannot be any residue or makeup on your lashes). I skipped the eye pads and petroleum jelly (vaseline) as even a small bit of petroleum jelly will only get on the lashes and prevent the product from adhering. 2) I applied the activator using the rounded end of a Q-tip, using the enclosed transfer pipet to apply activator to the q-tip. I spent a good 10 minutes applying activator to each eye (at least 20 mins total), thoroughly covering each lash from base to tip (I applied activator to the top side of my upper lashes as well as the underside). I only put a small amount of activator (no more than a few drops) on the q-tip each time (there should not be activator dripping off the q-tip), and I repeated this process until I had thoroughly coated every little bit of eachlash (and coated each lash multiple times). This way you can thoroughly coat each lash without getting activator in your eyes. 3) I knew that the pointed end of the q-tip was not going to work very well for applying the tint, so I used a tiny (no more than half an inch long), angled mascara wand specifically designed for applying mascara to the lashes in the corner of the eye. (I washed and dried the wand thoroughly before using to apply tint). My mascara wand came from my \\"Imju Fiberwig Tiny Sniper\\" mascara, but you could find a wand like this at most beauty supply stores like Sephora or Ulta (the wand should be very very tiny with the brush set at an angle). This was the perfect tool for applying the tint. I squeezed a small amount of tint onto a q-tip, then used the q-tip to apply the tint to the wand. As I did with the activator, I only applied a very small amount of tint at a time to avoid getting it in my eyes. I repeated the application of small amounts of tint until I had covered every bit of each lash, I also applied tint to both the top and bottom sides of my upper lashes. -By being very careful and applying only small amounts of tint at a time, I was able to avoid getting very much on my skin. The only place that I accidentally stained with tint was a small place on my upper eyelid right above the lash line in the outer corner (I usually smear mascara in the same spot by accident). But this is a very small place, it just looks like I have a bit of eyeliner on. I wiped the stain with a damp q-tip as soon as it happened, so it is very minor. I did not get any of the tint on the skin below my lashes, and I did not use any vaseline or the eye pads. After allowing the tint to dry for a few minutes, I washed my eyes with mild face wash (I use baby wash). My lashes are now a deep, rich black color! I still need mascara if I want them to be thicker and longer, but at least now they show up without anything on! This product works exactly as it says it will.The short list: -start with thoroughly clean and dry eyelashes, skip the vaseline under the eyes -only apply small amounts of activator at a time, but keep at it until you thoroughly coat each side of every lash (then coat each lash again) -use a tiny, angled (clean) mascara wand to apply the tint, only apply a small amount of tint at a time but repeat until every side of every lash is coated (apply to each lash from multiple sides) -go slowly and carefully, applying a small bit at a time; keep plenty of q-tips on hand to quickly wipe away mistakes Since I only applied a small amount of activator and tint at a time, I only got a little bit of the tint into my eyes, and it did sting, but luckily there was too little on my brush to cause any real pain. A few hours after application my eyes do feel a bit sensitive, sort of similar to the way they feel a few hours after chopping a strong onion or swimming in a chlorinated pool. I am expecting the tint to last for about 2&1/2-3 weeks, I will update this review if it lasts for a significantly shorter or longer period than expected. I am very picky about beauty products, but I plan on using this one again and again, and I highly recommend it.

  260. I have red hair and light eye lashes. I was getting tired doing the mascara ritual every morning before work, or before I would go out. I also hate when I get back home late, naturally tired, go to bed and get all comfortable only to realize I never took my mascara off... I was very intrigued when I came across this. I was a little nervous at the thought of putting chemicals near my eyes. I'm pretty clumsy and fumbly, so I was iffy about trying it out on myself. I went ahead and ordered it after reading in the reviews that a lot of people had no problems doing it on themselves with no help. I was reading several people saying the chemical stings their eyes when they were applying the mascara. I, thankfully, didn't experience any pain. I will say, the bottled labeled first solution is easy to apply and you don't have to worry about the staining at that point. Make sure you get all the lashes nice and wet with this stuff because if you don't, some lashes wont change colors. I used the q-tips that were provided. I did one eye at a time. I made sure to get all the lashes wet, and then I put more of the solution on the q-tip and did it again, just to be sure, and then let it set in for about a minute and a half. I made sure that I didn't have any of the first solution on my eye lid before applying the 2nd. As soon as I put the 2nd solution on the lashes, they instantly turned black. The lashes will clump together when you do this. It's perfectly fine if they do, just keep applying and make sure you get every lash. Once you rinse the solutions off and your lashes dry, they will separate back to normal. I let it set in for maybe 30 seconds, even though they say it's instant... I just wanted to make sure. I was pretty worried about how to rinse it off the lashes. Will it run and stain my face? Nope, it doesn't. All you have to do is cup water in your hand and basically hold your closed eye in the cupped water then let the water fall into the sink. I'd be careful notto rub your eye very much, and when drying- just gently pat your eyes dry. You will see some black come off on to the towel when patting your eye dry. I will say when I went to do my other eye, when I went to rinse it off, the lashes didn't get dyed. I have a feeling I must have still had some kind of oil or even makeup remover residue left in my lashes. Make sure your lashes are completely free of any residue from makeup or makeup remover/soap. The dye won't set in if you have anything on them. I rinsed that eye really good after that and tried again with success. I'm happy to say that after a month, my lashes are still dark and I haven't reapplied once! I would like to mention that this will not give your lashes the full effect that mascara gives, so if you lack length and volume in your lashes, you might be disappointed. I have long and full lashes, so I'm as happy as can be about it. When I would go without mascara, my eyes looked dull and people were constantly telling me I looked tired. Now that they are dark, I don't look sleepy and it looks very natural. I might do a re-apply in the next couple days. If you avoid rubbing your eyes and gently pat your eyes dry, you can get it to last a long time. Another note I would like to make: They come with these paper cut out face shield things to put under your eyes. You can cut them to the shape you want. They are annoying, so I didn't bother with them. The instructions say to use petroleum jelly on the skin under your eyes and eyelashes, so that your skin won't get stained by accident... I didn't do that because it sounded messy and if you accidentally get that stuff on your lashes, the dye won't take...so be careful when applying it you your face if you choose to use it...I just went without. I did get a little dye on a couple fingers and finger nails... My finger nails are still stained by it and the stains on my fingers just recently went away. I'll take a few stains on my hands in place of dealing with mascara every day! If you have light colored eyelashes, this product is definitely worth it. If you have dark lashes, don't waste your money or time, it will do nothing for you. This product does not add volume or length, just color.
